<p>The English <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">rock</a> group <a href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones" title="The Rolling Stones">The Rolling Stones</a> has released 29 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Studio_albums" title="Studio albums">studio albums</a>, 13 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Live_albums" title="Live albums">live albums</a>, 24 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Compilation_albums" title="Compilation albums">compilation albums</a>, three <a href="/wiki/Extended_play" title="Extended play">extended play singles</a>, and 107 <a href="/wiki/Single_(music)" title="Single (music)">singles</a>. The early albums and singles released from 1963 to 1967 were originally released on <a href="/wiki/Decca_Records" title="Decca Records">Decca Records</a> in the UK, and on their subsidiary label <a href="/wiki/London_Records" title="London Records">London Records</a> in the US.</p>
<p>It was common practice in the music industry prior to 1967 for British releases to be reconfigured for the American market. In some cases, the US version would be an entirely different album with different tracks, cover photos, liner notes, and so on. The first five British Rolling Stones albums were converted into seven LPs for American consumption, adding material from singles and the UK EPs. The two <i>Big Hits</i> singles packages, respectively from 1966 and 1969, differ in each nation, and in the case of <i><a href="/wiki/December%27s_Children_(And_Everybody%27s)" title="December's Children (And Everybody's)">December's Children (And Everybody's)</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Flowers_(The_Rolling_Stones_album)" title="Flowers (The Rolling Stones album)">Flowers</a></i>, there are no UK counterparts. This practice was quickly abandoned after <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a> insisted that their <a href="/wiki/Masterpiece" title="Masterpiece">magnum opus</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Sgt._Pepper%27s_Lonely_Hearts_Club_Band" title="Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band">Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band</a></i> be released internationally with identical track configurations and cover art.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> Rolling Stones' LP releases from <i><a href="/wiki/Their_Satanic_Majesties_Request" title="Their Satanic Majesties Request">Their Satanic Majesties Request</a></i> in 1967 forward are uniform in both the UK and the US, except for <i><a href="/wiki/Through_the_Past,_Darkly_(Big_Hits_Vol._2)" title="Through the Past, Darkly (Big Hits Vol. 2)">Through the Past, Darkly (Big Hits Vol. 2)</a></i>. The main difference between The Beatles' and The Rolling Stones' American discographies, were that The Rolling Stones configured their American albums themselves for London Records, whereas The Beatles had no say in tracklists for records released on <a href="/wiki/Capitol_Records" title="Capitol Records">Capitol Records</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Singles">Singles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Rolling_Stones_discography&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Singles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>In some cases the single's <a href="/wiki/A-side_and_B-side" title="A-side and B-side">B-side</a> charted separately; blank chart data indicates single not released in that nation. First single in the US is "<a href="/wiki/Not_Fade_Away_(song)" title="Not Fade Away (song)">Not Fade Away</a>" b/w "<a href="/wiki/I_Wanna_Be_Your_Man" title="I Wanna Be Your Man">I Wanna Be Your Man</a>", respectively the A-sides of the group's third and second singles in the UK.</li>
<li>Bracketed numbers next to chart positions denotes number of weeks spent in the individual chart.</li>
<li>On 19 August 1963, the band recorded "<a href="/wiki/Poison_Ivy_(song)" title="Poison Ivy (song)">Poison Ivy</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Fortune_Teller_(song)" title="Fortune Teller (song)">Fortune Teller</a>" to be their second single. A few hundred copies were pressed, but the single was withdrawn.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> These recordings would be included on the album <i>Saturday Club</i>, a compilation of tracks from various artists appearing on the Saturday Club (BBC radio) show of the time.</li>
</ul>
